Now, lemme tell ya, this place - wowee - this place is something else.

Didn't expect much going on, place was pretty much empty. But with a name like Zaytoon, you know something must be up.

Good vibes in the store - i order the fallafel deluxe. Side of pickles because I'm feeling dangerous.

Food came out in like 5 minutes and my oh my, this has got to be the biggest wrap in SF. SIZE MATTERS.

Tasted fantastic.

We also got fries. Fries were popping.

Pickles were popping.

Service was great - we got there late without realizing and they stayed open for us.

Zaytoon was popping.

Outdoor seating was a little sketch - table was so far out into the street I thought I was gonna get hit by a car a couple times, but hey - what's dinner without a little thrill?< /review>

< review>
Their lamb platter had a variety of flavors which makes this place taste unique and authentic. It may seem pricey at first since it is $13 a plate (as of 03/2020) but it is a lot of food and it was enough to fill me up. The lamb had a lot of the lamb fat smell which does not smell very good to me but if you do like it, good for you. The seasoned onions and cucumber tomato salad are fantastic though. I just wish that the price was lower but given the location it might not be possible.<//review>

< review>
I was desperately hungry so I took the nearest place that‚Äôs open. Saw no one inside so I asked him ‚Äúare you open?‚Äù  He said ‚Äúyeah, we‚Äôre just not busy.‚Äù

Sat down. The guy was more interested in browsing the tv for the right channel. Then he found his channel so he decided to glue his eyes to the screen.

<username>Kaajal Tiwary</username><Time>1593535427902<//Time><rating>5</rating>< Review>
I normally order groceries online. Due to the current pandemic, I found myself having to go to the store a few times to run my own errands. This store, I must say, has a good protocol in place for physical distancing procedures. They also took the temperature. Most of the  staff is friendly and helpful. There is one Sardar Ji at the cash counter. I think his name is Vir Singh. He always makes sure to ask if I found everything okay. I didn't find some vegetables yesterday. I thought they were out of stock. He asked me if I found everything. He then asked me to wait so he can check to see if they had it in the stock in the refrigerator in the back. Fortunately they  had it and it saved me a trip to another store. I like how they make sure the customers are taken care of. Will definitely go back when I need Indian groceries.<//Review>

It‚Äôs one stop shop. We used to get all our grocery from one stop. Price is comparative to other stores. Produce and dairy is fresh. They also sell fresh somosa and few other savories. I shopped here for over an year, almost every week.

Con

The staff are friendly, but also take things for granted. They run this rewards program that gives you 20$ credit after you hit a certain threshold. But when things go Hayward , say the system crashes - they would start over from beginning. To enroll for the program - you will need to write down some personal details on a sheet of paper. There is no clarity how the data will be handled later, or who uses it for what.

I once had a credit that they failed to honor since the system was reset due to the power outage. They knew me as regular customer, yet they failed to honor the credit. For me it was not about the 20$, but more about how they take things for granted. These kind of things are unacceptable in bigger stores , but it‚Äôs ok to happen in Indian store ?? I stopped going there ever since.

I‚Äôve given a poor rating due to my experience and disappointment.

If these kind of things are petty and does not matter, then the place is one stop grocery shop for you !<//Review>< date>
1579067004280</date>

<rate>5< /rate><review>I haven't seen any reviews for this place yet, which is surprising since they're really busy.

I will put a caveat on my 5 stars: I have gone to get my hair cut twice and Arielle, who cut my hair the first time, was really excellent so I made sure I went to her again. The 5-stars is mostly just for her since I haven't been to anyone else.

The shop itself is really nice, bright, clean, organized and everything is new so that's all good. Everyone is really friendly, also nice. The entrance/waiting area is pretty cramped, but I have never been there long so I haven't had that bother me. You can check in through an app to avoid having to wait. And if there's a long wait there are nearby shops you can probably go look around and I'd recommend it. They have the waiting list displayed on the wall TV too so you can see where you're at in line.

Again I cannot review the other stylists, but I will say that I would personally be nervous having any of them cut my hair because both times I was there someone accidentally "checked-out" and changed my notes in the computer while I was still getting my haircut. They're supposed to check you in when you get there and check you out when they finish so they can put in the computer how you like your hair cut for next time, but since they all use the same register it seems some of the stylists get confused and check out the wrong person. I could understand it the first time when they had just opened but it's been a few months and I have reservations about having someone cut my hair if they can't use the register.

Still, for the price on the coupons they have right now (because they recently opened) it's definitely worth a try to see if you can find a stylist who cuts hair the way you like.</review>< pics>
None</pics>

Checkout is laid out poorly with the new guidelines.  Lines tend to form both down merchandise aisles and at 90 degree angles perpendicular to the checkout lanes.  In order to get into a line down a cluttered merchandise aisle, you may have to go all the way back to the meat department and then U-turn back towards the checkout.  By the time you get there, that line may be replaced by the 90 degree formation and you may need to start over back at the meat department.  The one-size-fits-all Karens who do not take into account the length of a shopping cart in social distancing and who are unable to clinically process the awkwardness of life in general tend to hide out in the merchandise aisles far from the checkout, forming the less-than-obvious lines much greater than six feet away where markings are not present.  These people start "cutting-in-line" arguments with those who process information differently, who form lines based on the markings on the floor.  I work in busy pharmacy departments where strict social distancing isn't possible and neither is it possible at Stater Bros.  I recognize that and it's OK, because it is what it is and the risk is extremely low.  Stater Bros. shouldn't pretend otherwise and contribute to the problem.  This Karen abuse from other shoppers with no clinical disease experience is out of control and I need to avoid this condition until somebody there figures this out.  The threat of arguments from these people is a high risk condition I cannot afford.  Unlike my new other sources that do not seem have these problems to a significant degree, Stater Bros. continues to be out of many supplies, so it's getting easier to consider going elsewhere.<//review>
